<div id="review_521924604" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521924604" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/521924604?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer521924604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12607753775020473477"><i>
  <b>3.5 STARS<br/><blockquote>Not that I had a ton of experience but this was the freakiest slumber party I'd ever attended.</blockquote></b>
</i><br/>I think I came into this book expecting something entirely different from how it turned out to be. Some turned out better but more just left me unsatisfied. <br/><br/>The story starts with Lela and Nadia forging the unlikeliest of friendships: Lela is the school misfit who smokes, does push ups and beats up abusive foster fathers while Nadia is the school's Queen Bee. They meet in the most auspicious</span>
  <span id="freeText12607753775020473477" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>3.5 STARS<br><blockquote>Not that I had a ton of experience but this was the freakiest slumber party I'd ever attended.</blockquote></b>
</i><br>I think I came into this book expecting something entirely different from how it turned out to be. Some turned out better but more just left me unsatisfied. <br><br>The story starts with Lela and Nadia forging the unlikeliest of friendships: Lela is the school misfit who smokes, does push ups and beats up abusive foster fathers while Nadia is the school's Queen Bee. They meet in the most auspicious manner, Lela saving Nadia from getting her stash from an opportunistic drug dealer. It seems like a sweet story of Nadia taking Lela under her wing and giving her a shiny new perspective in life, a camera and the daring to forge a future out for herself... until Nadia commits suicide and gets herself sent to The Dark City where... hmm.. it's actually quite fuzzy the workings of this place but think of it as purgatory with shady creatures that possess already dead bodies, where you can watch your least liked episodes of your favorite shows through a TV connected to an umbilical cord (!) and a tower that eats people. Literally.<br><br>Lela has to find Nadia and manages to entail the help of Malachi, the captain of the Guards who watches over this magical, fun place.<br><br>I liked a lot about this book. I liked the crafty imagination vividly depicting the details and the dreariness of The Dark City. There was a lot of action sequences which I quite enjoyed, the gruesome details appealed to the latent action flick fanboy in me. I have some fondness over Michael because he reminds me of Fat Bastard and I really liked Ana because often times she spoke in my behalf when I wanted to voice out my disbelief over certain plot points. I also liked how the author handled the issues of suicide, depression and rape making the behavior of those who experienced it in this book believable, earning my compassion and understanding.<br><br>I just didn't expect it to be this... SUGARY. I don't mind the sweetness of it all, I just needed something more to wash off the cloying taste. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380407477ra/795871.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's so easy to use romance as the gateway emotion to form the foundation of a story. I'm okay with that, even if it sometimes comes to a point where it starts to feel lazy and this book crossed that line several times over, I felt, relying too much on the chemistry between Malachi and Lela to drive the story along.<br><br>I really like Malachi, his story is heartbreaking, but as Lela romantic interest he got a little too whipped for my taste.<br><br>Thinking back, it wasn't really insta-love but the gradual attraction between Lela and Malachi felt flimsy to me. Overall, Malachi seemed drawn to Lela by her strength and tenacity in the face of a daunting situation. Which is not bad... until he dropped all his responsibilities to do everything in his power to help this "fascinating" creature and thus single-handedly founding The Cult of Lela. I just wish the romance wasn't as heavy handed as it ended up (I can't believe I'm complaining about that) because it felt like an ill-fit for me in the face of how crazy-impressive the world Sarah Fine built here.<br><br>Crazy-impressive but still confusing. The scope just felt too big and tied to too many contradicting mythologies. I have this picture of Suicide City as some purgatory where you work out your issues and when you're ready, you go to The Sanctum and get judged if you can move on to the next phase. This made the ending sound a lot like cheating. Because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don't get the deal with Lela taking Nadia's place so she can go into the grassy, sunshiny place and have her soul move on <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. That's like getting someone to take the exam for you while you go on a vacation. Maybe my preconceived notions about purgatory colored my confusion further but the logic of it all looked pretty skewed to me.<br><br>I'm very vanilla towards Lela. I liked her in the beginning but towards the middle she started to call herself out on her mistakes. She'd openly declare herself stupid or a moron out loud... but her awareness of this doesn't change the fact that she did get the stupid on in some scenes. I think my tipping point was this very Matrix-y sequence (which I liked) where she gets taught how to fight by Malachi and Ana only <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[to burn her hand during crunch time thus making the flirty fighting lessons pointless <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br>I'm not even going to get started on the Mazikin (seriously, what are those things?) and the vagueness of these creatures. Suffice to say, I'm terribly disappointed with what I know of them in the end. It's okay to withhold some of the plot points for the next book, but seeing the big role they played in this book, what I knew of them by the last page was terribly deficient and didn't really spark my curiosity any more than it confused me.<br><br>Despite these gaping plot holes and the rough journey to get there, I still liked how things ended. I'm still curious where things are going and how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Malachi and Lela <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> would figure in the new status quo. I'm hopeful the wrinkles in the plot would get ironed out sufficiently and if I can dare hope further, ease on the sugar a little, maybe.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12607753775020473477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503465535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9169375978387178480"><a href='http://booknook.me/sanctum-by-sarah-fine/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404719i/787817._SX540_.jpg' alt='Sanctum by Sarah Fine - Don't confuse what you want with what you need' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b><a href='http://booknook.me/sanctum-by-sarah-fine/' rel='nofollow noopener'>BookNook</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br/><br/>Oh my god, you guys!!! I did not expect this book to be so <em>amazing</em>. I bought this book completely on a whim. I never do that. I saw an ad for it on my Kindle screensaver, thought <em>"That's kind of a cool cover,"</em> and bought it. <strong>Well, <em>Sanctum</em> blew me away.</strong><br/><br/>I think I'm going to burst if I don't mention the romance right away, because it was incredible. <strong>I didn't expect a great romance from a paranormal story.</strong> Usually when I want a great romance, I look towards con</span>
  <span id="freeText9169375978387178480" style="display:none"><a href="http://booknook.me/sanctum-by-sarah-fine/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404719i/787817._SX540_.jpg" alt="Sanctum by Sarah Fine - Don't confuse what you want with what you need" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b><a href="http://booknook.me/sanctum-by-sarah-fine/" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNook</a> — Young Adult book reviews</b><br><br>Oh my god, you guys!!! I did not expect this book to be so <em>amazing</em>. I bought this book completely on a whim. I never do that. I saw an ad for it on my Kindle screensaver, thought <em>"That's kind of a cool cover,"</em> and bought it. <strong>Well, <em>Sanctum</em> blew me away.</strong><br><br>I think I'm going to burst if I don't mention the romance right away, because it was incredible. <strong>I didn't expect a great romance from a paranormal story.</strong> Usually when I want a great romance, I look towards contemporaries. But <em>
  <strong>Sanctum</strong>
</em> has it all: great plot, great world building, and an insanely delicious and jaw-dropping romance. Honestly, the romance does start off a little fast, but I seriously did not care at all. <strong>Because Malachi—oh-so-sexy Malachi—is the sweetest, sexiest, most badass of all book boyfriends.</strong><br><br><blockquote>The deep voids of his eyes were surrounded by thick, black lashes and full of confidence and threat. It was as if he'd already assessed my weaknesses and ticked off all the possible ways to kill me, so now he could relax and be friendly.</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>"I never said I didn't want you to touch me! That is exactly the problem. Every time you put your hands on me, I don't want you to let go.</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>"You can be selfish. It makes me feel wanted. And I..." He chuckled softly. "I want you to want me."</blockquote><br><br>Malachi is sweet, selfless, tender, but also the hot Captain of the Guard that can kill guys with his bare hands. He's deep and thoughtful, but without being corny or cheesy. <strong>So many of the scenes with Malachi—especially towards the end—had me giggling and squealing like a crazy, love-struck girl!</strong><br><br>Okay, I'll attempt to pull myself together and talk about Lela. <strong>Lela was a fantastic main character, and extremely likeable (most of the time).</strong> She's strong, sensitive, damaged, and also kicks some ass. I loved her dedication to Nadia. It was just so... admirable. <strong>At times it made me feel bad, because I seriously wondered if I would go through all that for one of my friends.</strong> I mean, we'd all like to think we would, but if it comes down to it, would we actually give up eternal happiness to travel through hell (with no guarantee that we could go back)? I really think this makes Lela one of the most selfless characters I've ever read about.<br><br>But the thing I loved most about Lela was how she held her own. She wasn't a poor, pathetic, wimpy character that needed rescuing. <strong>Lela was strong, stubborn, and determined.</strong> Sure, sometimes she was a little foolish, or maybe a little too self-sacrificing, but I still loved how independent she was. She makes some incredibly difficult choices that had me sitting there in awe.<br><br><strong><em>Sanctum</em> is one of those books that will have you highlighting every other line.</strong> It is riddled with deep, thought-provoking messages about life, death, loss, and love. So many passages forced me to just stop and think for a minute. <strong>I swear, you guys, this shit is deep.</strong><br><br><blockquote>They're so absorbed in their own sadness that they can't see past the darkness.</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>She once told me that everybody carried their secret savages beneath their skin, and some people just covered them better than others.</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>I think some people like the disease better [than the cure]. It's more familiar, and they don't want to give it up, even once they know they can be healed of it.</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>"Mercy is not a right. Mercy is a gift from one to another. It can't be earned."</blockquote><br><br>I kind of expected <em>
  <strong>Sanctum</strong>
</em> to be good, just because of the high ratings, but I don't think I expected it to be <em>this</em> good. <strong><em>Sanctum</em> was so imaginative, dark, scary, and provocative.</strong> It has a deliciously swoony romance that will bring you to your knees, and is riddled with tough decisions and sacrifices. Book 2: bring it on. (Seriously, I want it now, please.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9169375978387178480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Ails" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12873266-ails"><img alt="Ails" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351577137p2/12873266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452139098?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ails" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ails" href="/user/show/12873266-ails">Ails</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16155240-sanctum">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jan Bethel, Ira, Jill, Lexie, Erika, Stephanie, everyone! </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=swoon-worthy">swoon-worthy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=badass-female">badass-female</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452139098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12621829178039736809"><i>
  <b>"My plan: Get into the city. Get Nadia. Keep us safe. Find a way out. Simple." </b>
</i> <br/><br/>IT'S BEEN A LOOOONG TIME SINCE I FELT THE <i>RUSH</i> OF ADRENALINE FROM READING A BOOK. I miss it. I need it. I am <i>
  <b>C-R-A-V-I-N-G</b>
</i> for it. Craving for that pumped up feeling and the need to stay up late merely because I can't put it down.<br/><br/>THANK GOD I STUMBLED UPON THIS BOOK. <br/><br/>I'm not going to lie. If it wasn't for 'Angelfall,' I wouldn't have found & read Sanctum. I googled "Books similar to Angelfall on goodreads" (<i>Oh</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12621829178039736809" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"My plan: Get into the city. Get Nadia. Keep us safe. Find a way out. Simple." </b>
</i> <br><br>IT'S BEEN A LOOOONG TIME SINCE I FELT THE <i>RUSH</i> OF ADRENALINE FROM READING A BOOK. I miss it. I need it. I am <i>
  <b>C-R-A-V-I-N-G</b>
</i> for it. Craving for that pumped up feeling and the need to stay up late merely because I can't put it down.<br><br>THANK GOD I STUMBLED UPON THIS BOOK. <br><br>I'm not going to lie. If it wasn't for 'Angelfall,' I wouldn't have found &amp; read Sanctum. I googled "Books similar to Angelfall on goodreads" (<i>Ohhh yes, I'm SUCH a fan..</i>) and saw Sanctum on top of the list. But hey, <b>don't get me wrong</b>, this isn't about angels and apocalypse at all. It's just similarly oh-so-good, adrenaline rushing, BADASS, &amp; has a GOOD ROMANCE that isn't easy to find nowadays.<br><br>■■■<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397067i/765868.jpg" width="500" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(photo from p0m.deviantart.com)<br><br>The majority of the book takes place behind the Suicide Gates called the "Dark City." It's a place afterlife where those who commit suicide go. The city is bathed in darkness and all sources of light are lifeless and faint. A city where you can see the sun at <i>zero</i> brightness &amp; warmth. A city where dead people breathe, bleed, and can get "killed."<br><br>Oh, have I mentioned there are creepy, filthy, and venomous human monsters roaming in this city?.... Go figure.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391479ra/753899.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <b>"I liked being in control. It was why I hated pills. And alcohol. And most grown-ups. Staying one step ahead was the only way to keep myself from getting hurt again."</b>
</i><br><br>Meet Lela Santos. She's by far the <u>strongest</u> and bravest girl among all my favorite female characters. I'm telling you, she's a real SPITFIRE. And boy, does she kick ass!<br><br><i>
  <b>"That’s better, thank you. Now, if you don’t tell me why you’re here, right now, I will slice that tattoo off your arm and burn it in front of you, Lela."</b>
</i><br><br>Meet Malachi, the captain of the guards. <i>**His features were smooth and unlined but it held a harsh, dangerous sort of beauty.**</i> He isn't a bad boy. He isn't a good boy either. He is dangerous, at the same time sympathetic. He doesn't often say the sweetest words to Lela (<i>thank God!</i>) but he never hides how <i>
  <b>much</b>
</i> he's come to care about her either. <i>Aww Malachi, you're my kind of perfect.. *dreamy sigh* </i><br><br> Malachi and Lela's chemistry is just <b>undeniable</b>. It's not often that a love story really strikes a cord within me but THIS.. THE ROMANCE, I FEEL IT ALL THE WAY TO MY BONES. (<i>You guys don't have any idea how much I want to insert scenes &amp; dialogues to support this but I want you all to read them firsthand</i>)<br> <br> ❤ ❥ ❤ ❥ ❤ <br><br>Sarah Fine's writing is sooo vivid, it's <b>AMAZING</b>. The world in this book is <i>fully fleshed out</i> that I promise there's not a scene I hadn't pictured in my head. I could see and <i>
  <b>feel</b>
</i> everything that was happening. Also, the plot never lost momentum despite the great romance going on. I appreciate that <i>A LOT</i>. <br><br>Overall, I love the originality of the story, the writing, the characters, the danger, the imperfections, EVERYTHING. <b>I'm recommending this to everyone!!!</b></span>

<div id="review_455091411" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/455091411" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/455091411?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer455091411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14756382437994195807"><b>Holy Moly!</b> It’s been ages and ages and ages since a YA PNR’s (UF?) left me feeling this pumped. She’s dark and broken and fancies herself damaged, but is also moving passed that. She’s friends and connections and finally sees something more out there for her. ‘Till she loses her someone and finds herself in this twisted version of not-quite-hell, maybe purgatory. <br/><br/>It’s twisted this place: getting all you want but never being happy with whatever that happens to be! It’s twisted this place with the</span>
  <span id="freeText14756382437994195807" style="display:none"><b>Holy Moly!</b> It’s been ages and ages and ages since a YA PNR’s (UF?) left me feeling this pumped. She’s dark and broken and fancies herself damaged, but is also moving passed that. She’s friends and connections and finally sees something more out there for her. ‘Till she loses her someone and finds herself in this twisted version of not-quite-hell, maybe purgatory. <br /><br />It’s twisted this place: getting all you want but never being happy with whatever that happens to be! It’s twisted this place with these guards shepherding these people so despondent, they’re totally unaware of where they are and or even <i>why</i> they are! Setting of my nightmares, this place where things could only have been worse had it been filled with a Pennywise here, some flying paper monkeys there. But fascinating too with the in’s and out’s of growing buildings and towers that consume those in it! <br /><br />And while I loved the world she’d found herself in (I was enthralled by it all, in fact) Lena and Malachi and the rest of them were not bad either. She’s kick ass, he’s kicks… hell, they were all kick ass if not a bit deluded over their own importance. With that last minor thing aside, the darkness they each brought with them piqued my interest as they came in to the story on equal footing:<br /><br />It’s not boy saves girl or girl inspires boy, though things could have gone that way, too. Here he’s broken and dark, but she is too. It’s just that he’s had more time dealing while she’s new to that... and OK so he mentors her and takes her under his wing, (and may be I could have done with out that,) but the closer she got to doing what she was there for, the closer they got to each other! So that the chemistry going on (and there’s no denying the chemistry there,) was a lot like Dimka and his Rose, less the whole forbidden love thing the latter had going for them.<br /><br />But my favorite things here and note that there were several things in this... Well, the first touches on her being kick ass… but not <i>just</i> kick ass. A couple of moments have her showing vulnerability so that it’s obvious… her being the way she is, well, there’s reason for that. Just think of Chessie or Eve and you’ll see a little of them in her. Another is how she gets called out on being full of it…though not necessarily in those terms and not as harshly. She rides to the rescue only to be told that there’s a time and place for everything and everyone, herself included.<br /><br /><b>Awesome…</b> and that’s even when the lead characters were behaving like douches!<br /><br /><b>4/5</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14756382437994195807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1186864121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1186864121" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1186864121?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1186864121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15352945615569967052">Not what I expected at all.<br/><br/>I thought maybe this would be a fantasy journey into a Dante-like hell that a girl goes through to find her friend. Instead, it was a story about depression, suicide, abuse, and overcoming. I was struck by how well the author was able to explore such dark and depressing subjects without depressing the reader. Instead of feeling sad and hopeless by the despair that is so well depicted, I felt encouraged by the overall message of fighting to overcome the past and to keep</span>
  <span id="freeText15352945615569967052" style="display:none">Not what I expected at all.<br /><br />I thought maybe this would be a fantasy journey into a Dante-like hell that a girl goes through to find her friend. Instead, it was a story about depression, suicide, abuse, and overcoming. I was struck by how well the author was able to explore such dark and depressing subjects without depressing the reader. Instead of feeling sad and hopeless by the despair that is so well depicted, I felt encouraged by the overall message of fighting to overcome the past and to keep going no matter what. <br /><br />Lela personified this message. She had her rock-bottom. She saw a glimpse of hell and she fought back. She gives credit to Nadia for encouraging her to bringing her back, but she gets credit for even allowing Nadia to get even close to her. It takes so much courage to let another person in when you have suffered abuse because this is so true about what you are thinking when you reveal yourself to another person:<br /><br /><i>Should I have kept my mouth shut? Would he look at me differently now that all he'd suspected had been confirmed?<br />...I didn't want to be damaged. I wanted... to see me as whole. Not broken. Not used...</i><br /><br />That passage is only one of so many that I highlighted in this book because it really was amazing at how well the author captured the psyche of the depressed, abused, and suicidal. <b>With one big exception</b>, and that was how quickly she seemed to be able to accept Malachi's touch without many problems. Malachi was an exceptional character - he had been working with depressed and suicide victims for many years and really understood their mind-set - but still. I wasn't so sure about how quickly Lela fell for him. <br /><br />The world-building in this book is also really great. I loved how this place was a whole new fantasy world, instead of building on something that we already know (such as Dante). All in all, it was a great adventure through an interesting world alongside this amazing message.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15352945615569967052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1097606231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097606231" />
    <a title="Ashleyjo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33970054-ashleyjo"><img alt="Ashleyjo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466919724p2/33970054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097606231?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleyjo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleyjo" href="/user/show/33970054-ashleyjo">Ashleyjo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097606231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15361111042104693912">For paranormal romance/action, this book was 5 bright, twinkling stars! <br/><br/>The plot was engaging, begging each page to be turned to find out the fate of all the characters and delve deeper into the world. No lulls... Every moment is pushing the action, blooming emotional attachments, or overall plot forward. <br/><br/>The world was realistically imaginative, captivating, & yet scary as hell (literally) without being all brimstone and fire. I absolutely love an author that's able to give and <i>show</i> readers a wo</span>
  <span id="freeText15361111042104693912" style="display:none">For paranormal romance/action, this book was 5 bright, twinkling stars! <br /><br />The plot was engaging, begging each page to be turned to find out the fate of all the characters and delve deeper into the world. No lulls... Every moment is pushing the action, blooming emotional attachments, or overall plot forward. <br /><br />The world was realistically imaginative, captivating, &amp; yet scary as hell (literally) without being all brimstone and fire. I absolutely love an author that's able to give and <i>show</i> readers a world throughout the plot &amp; characters verses going into long diatribes, inner monologues, or descriptive narratives that <i>tell</i> the reader about the world, and this author did it perfectly! <br /><br />Each character had a unique and interesting voice and history. Their backstories were heartbreaking, especially Malachi's, and gave reason to their strengths and determination. These are characters that have seen the worst of humanity. <br /><br />Lela was fierce, brave, &amp; loyal, placing her friendship with Nadia &amp; growing love for Malachi above her own needs and wants. Malachi was the epitome of swoon - badass that softened only in the arms of the gal that had suddenly captured his heart. <br /><br />Highly recommend for paranormal readers that like equal parts action and developing romance. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15361111042104693912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_460186552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460186552" />
    <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue"><img alt="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185382p2/4659650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460186552?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=why-am-i-just-now-reading-this">why-am-i-just-now-reading-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=souls-afterlife">souls-afterlife</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460186552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6494181242156616713">Where the hell was I when this book was released last year?  Seriously.  The only reason it was even on my radar was because of a <a href='http://thestrangestsituation.blogspot.com/2012/12/introducing-malachis-journal-and-chance.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>blog tour</a> wherein I believe parts of <a href='http://guardsoftheshadowlands.tumblr.com/tagged/Malachi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Malachi's journal were revealed</a>.  [I still need to check those out, so don't spoil anything for me.  ;)]  And apparently, Amazon Children's Publishing is touting this as their <a href='http://cleareyesfullshelves.com/blog/ala2013' rel='nofollow noopener'>next big thing</a> for fans of Susan Ee's <i>Angelfall</i>.  As a <a href='http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/01/audiobook-review-angelfall-by-susan-ee.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>HUGE fan</a> of that book, I can tell you that <i>Sanctum</i> was just as good as <i>Angelfall</i>.<br/><br/>While <i>Angelfall</i> enter</span>
  <span id="freeText6494181242156616713" style="display:none">Where the hell was I when this book was released last year?  Seriously.  The only reason it was even on my radar was because of a <a href="http://thestrangestsituation.blogspot.com/2012/12/introducing-malachis-journal-and-chance.html" rel="nofollow noopener">blog tour</a> wherein I believe parts of <a href="http://guardsoftheshadowlands.tumblr.com/tagged/Malachi" rel="nofollow noopener">Malachi's journal were revealed</a>.  [I still need to check those out, so don't spoil anything for me.  ;)]  And apparently, Amazon Children's Publishing is touting this as their <a href="http://cleareyesfullshelves.com/blog/ala2013" rel="nofollow noopener">next big thing</a> for fans of Susan Ee's <i>Angelfall</i>.  As a <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/01/audiobook-review-angelfall-by-susan-ee.html" rel="nofollow noopener">HUGE fan</a> of that book, I can tell you that <i>Sanctum</i> was just as good as <i>Angelfall</i>.<br /><br />While <i>Angelfall</i> entertains the idea of deviant angels on earth, <i>Sanctum</i> takes the story to the afterlife.  I know, I know...angels and the afterlife are soooo overdone in YA.  But it's the author's spin that makes these books really stand apart from all of those others.  With <i>Sanctum</i>, there's no going through the stages of grief after death, no wishing to be alive again.  This book is simply about Lela's mission to save her suicidal best friend from a hellish future in the afterlife, one that she's only dreamt about but that her friend is truly living.<br /><br />Lela hasn't had an easy life.  And until she sticks her neck out for someone she doesn't even know, she hadn't realized it could actually get better.  Once Nadia befriends Lela, everything changes.  Suddenly, Lela has a future.  But just when things are going great, Nadia leaves Lela to deal with everything on her own.  Lela didn't set out to follow Nadia into the afterlife, but now that she's there, and because she knows what awaits Nadia thanks to the nightmares that have plagued her over the years, she is willing to do anything to save her best friend.  I think it speaks so much to Lela's character and to how much she's progressed that she cares so deeply for this girl that she's only known for a year.<br /><br />The afterlife doesn't have to be the muted, dreary existence that awaits Nadia behind the Suicide Gates. But as the name implies, that is the afterlife that one can expect when they take their own life.  The cover of this book might have turned me off previously because of its bleakness, but now, having read the book, I think it's a very appropriate and entirely suitable cover.  The setting of this story is so dismal and gray, but based on the descriptions provided by Lela in the book, the city depicted on the cover is exactly like I imagined.  And knowing how it got that way makes it all the more intriguing because this is a place where you can have anything you want but it will never be enough.<br /><br />While searching this dark city for Nadia so that she can break her out, Lela has a run-in with one of the guards.  I don't know any better way to describe their relationship than this:  Malachi is to Lela what Dimitri was to Rose in the Vampire Academy series...sexy accent included.  Lela is already strong and capable, but Malachi makes her better.  In Malachi, Lela finds the sanctuary and solace that she has desperately needed all her life.  But Lela means just as much to Malachi...after learning his story and how he ended up at the Suicide Gates, I think he might need Lela even more than she needs him.<br /><br />Malachi agrees to help Lela find Nadia and get them out of the city, but there are risks involved.  There are these creatures (souls?) called Mazakin that want to be set free, and they are invading the Shadowlands.  I like what this storyline added to the book:  the danger, the race to stop them, the uneasy feeling that it might already be too late.  I feel like maybe there's a reason why Lela followed Nadia so quickly in death, that the powers that be have a purpose for Lela, and maybe it has something to do with stopping the Mazakin.  I usually am not a fan of taking free will away from a character, but in this case, it works.<br /><br />Know what else is working for this story?  The audiobook narrator.  Amy McFadden is <i>perrrrrfect</i>!  All of the accents, the emotion she expresses...I liken her skills to that of Khristine Hvam, who provided the narration for a couple of the Vampire Academy books (coincidence?) and Laini Taylor's <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bones</i> series.  This audiobook was so unbelievably good; it's the kind that you could listen to over and over again.  Or maybe I'm just jonesing for another Malachi fix.<br /><br />I could go on and on about this book, and still not fully convey how much I loved it.  It's equal parts dark and disturbing, but there's an underlying current of hopefulness throughout.  The tender moments far outweigh the battles scenes as far as favorites go for me because the chemistry between Malachi and Lela is undeniable, but that doesn't mean I can't appreciate how badass these characters are.  I'm so very glad I found this sleeper hit when I did...before it exploded on the YA market like <i>Angelfall</i> did.  And although I hope the book follows in those same footsteps and exceeds everyone's expectations, one place I hope it doesn't tread is the no-man's land of "<i>Is she <b>ever</b> going to write the sequel?</i>"  Because it's a whole other kind of torture to be waiting for the second book <i>when there's no release date in sight</i>.  (By the by, there's no cliffhanger, if that's what you're thinking.  I simply loved this story and want more.  Like yesterday.)<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes:</b><br /><br />"He looked up at me, dark brown eyes shining. "You're so beautiful," he slurred making me sure his lips were growing numb and his brain wasn't far behind. <i>Figures. The first time a guy tells me I'm beautiful, I'm in hell and he's delirious.</i><br /><br />"This kiss was a living thing. A wild and dangerous thing. It spread its wings and carried us out over the city, over the walls. Malachi tasted like the forest, like the sun, like every dream I'd ever had about what this moment should be."<br /><br />"I wanted the chance to give him something, to give him the best of me, as pathetic as it was, damaged and broken, warped at the edges, hardly worth having. I decided that if I had the chance, if he asked, if he needed, it was his."<br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/02/audiobook-review-sanctum-by-sarah-fine.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6494181242156616713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9622673349244991751">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Sanctum was a thrilling I want to gobble you up in one sitting type of book. But lo and behold the time I decided to pick it up, it was as if the world was conspiring against me. It took me five days to finish this book, and by the end of these five days my nails were ruggedly bitten.<br/><br/>Sarah Fine gave us a world full of despair, a world where no one wants to go to by choice, but this is what our MC Lela decides to do. Her best friend Nadia who meant the world to her has taken her life, Le</span>
  <span id="freeText9622673349244991751" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Sanctum was a thrilling I want to gobble you up in one sitting type of book. But lo and behold the time I decided to pick it up, it was as if the world was conspiring against me. It took me five days to finish this book, and by the end of these five days my nails were ruggedly bitten.<br /><br />Sarah Fine gave us a world full of despair, a world where no one wants to go to by choice, but this is what our MC Lela decides to do. Her best friend Nadia who meant the world to her has taken her life, Lela is really distraught about it. Nadia was there for Lela when she needed her the most, without her, she never would have become who she is today. It also doesn’t help that Lela keeps having visions of Nadia; all she wants to do is get her back any way possible. But she didn’t believe that she actually could.<br /><br />Lela was such a head strong girl; I liked her strong will and determination to do anything to get Nadia back. The world she found herself in, I know for a fact that I would never survive, but many a times with her back against the wall Lela came out fighting. Malachi, where do I even start with this fine specimen? I remember a lot of my blogging friends were really enthusiastic about his character and it really is easy to see why. He was also such a tough individual, but I think what makes me melt even over guys is when they show their soft vulnerable side. Many times we were given insights into this other side of Malachi and at times it really broke my heart. Malachi certainly left a lasting impression with me, that I’m sure my blogging friends who have seemed to already have claimed him will have a fight on their hands.<br /><br />Sanctum is another book this year which truly surprised me, it’s not a book which I would have immediately picked up but I’m so glad that I finally did. Sarah Fine has created a gem of a read, with pulsating scenes, a beautiful romance and difficult decisions for characters to make. In a way it’s good that I waited a while to pick up Sanctum as I only have to wait two months before I can get my hands on Fractured. <br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_521435877" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521435877" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5744962-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363829197p2/5744962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/521435877?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/5744962-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anna by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=death-grieve">death-grieve</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=men">men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5744962-anna?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer521435877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2396918738547615406"><br/>Anybody familiar with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5031312.Dante_Alighieri' title='Dante Alighieri' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dante Alighieri</a>'s <i>The Divine Comedy</i> where the dead's soul or afterlife moves along whether in the gates of heaven; the fires of hell; or to wait in purgatory. These are the state where in theory we thought might happen. In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5752145.Sarah_Fine' title='Sarah Fine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah Fine</a>'s paranormal fiction series, Guards of the Shadowlands, she created a world like you'd never imagine, where when somebody dies in their own will would be most likely to arrive at the Suicide Gates armed with huge, armored guards, and wandering </span>
  <span id="freeText2396918738547615406" style="display:none"><br>Anybody familiar with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5031312.Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri" rel="nofollow noopener">Dante Alighieri</a>'s <i>The Divine Comedy</i> where the dead's soul or afterlife moves along whether in the gates of heaven; the fires of hell; or to wait in purgatory. These are the state where in theory we thought might happen. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5752145.Sarah_Fine" title="Sarah Fine" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Fine</a>'s paranormal fiction series, Guards of the Shadowlands, she created a world like you'd never imagine, where when somebody dies in their own will would be most likely to arrive at the Suicide Gates armed with huge, armored guards, and wandering souls pent at their own suffering. It's not a picture of heaven nor hell and neither was it some place to expiate ones sin. <br><br>The Suicide City plays a major setting with our heroine, Lela, to find the friend that means every waking, breathing second of her life. She wanders through a labyrinth of the dead's wants, needs, and desires that surrounds all over the city - that builds and expands - when humans wished it to be. Through there she went about seeing more and knowing little of the place. She made serious choices and grave decisions just to save and somehow steer her friend from what would have been an implacable damage.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Tell me before you go. I really want to know. Why would you give up your chance at happiness to come to what you knew was a horrible place? Why would you do that, knowing she <i>chose</i> to kill herself? To leave you and everyone else who loved her? Why would you come after her and trap yourself here when she made such a choice?"</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I also want to ask her that. Why go through <b>all</b> that's about to happen just for Nadia? But then she gave us her reason. She lets us be inside her and make us feel what she felt when she's with her. She lets us see the full-frontal feeling of what it's like be cherished and admired of what and who she really is. So I guess it's only fair she'd do it despite enduring the machinations. To quote her: <b>"The things I do for friendship."</b> I were in her situation though, I don't think I could do it. I would live for the life one would never have and that's probably something I'd do for somebody. That said, I give her enough credit for being bold and brave.<br><br>In the quest of Lela's search, she meets these people she'd grown fascination to. Those who would also be willing to bet their lives and responsibilities just for her sole purpose. Malachi is what you may call a knight and shining armor. His character, though we'd usually come across this kind of hero, somehow has a different zing to it. His sterling disposition is not hard to miss and surely ain't easy to forget. I wholly admire what he's capable of doing, what he'd come upon to encounter, and most especially, what he'd experienced and gone through in what became of him. Seldom have I read wherein the second most important character had a troubling back-story so you could only imagine what I felt when I read something about Malachi's past. Other than him, I thought Ana was a great character too. She's quite resilient and intense, though I was saddened of what happened to her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No spoiler. :) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Surprisingly, I was baffled that although this was kind of a fantasy book, it did not shift away from the realistic idea. The characters, if not most of the time, would greatly experience and reflect in their emotions. The talk of depression, dying, or something to do with the psychological, physical or mental sense was highly present and notable. It was really something I was glad to look forward to while reading. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Some people <i>can't</i> keep fighting. Some people want to escape. Some people are not ready - are not able - to find a way for deal with what's in front of them. Sometimes there's no one to help them. Sometimes they don't know how to ask for help. Sometimes it feels like there's no choice but to end it. No other way out. And sometimes it's impossible to see past that.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>This book, I tell you is super fun. And it's quite dark, but only a little bit. It's a different take on a paranormal/urban fantasy-ish story with an astounding new world and characters you would greatly admire. It's full of adventure and thrill so I'm sure everyone's good to go. I foresee this series will be great and I'll be there to witness it all.<br><br><br>*A shout-out to my wonderful, spirited buddy-read, <b>Stacia</b>, for doing this with me. Though it took us a while to finish, but I really had fun. I'd be happy to do this again, soon! <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406717ra/793886.gif" alt="descripion/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>**Can't get enough of Malachi? Well me either so here's some treat the author was so kind to make: <a> Malachi's journals</a>. Be sure to check this out after you read the first book. <br><br><br><br><br><br><br>xx</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2396918738547615406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_426585900" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426585900" />
    <a title="Kristy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2705039-kristy"><img alt="Kristy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453228324p2/2705039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426585900?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristy" href="/user/show/2705039-kristy">Kristy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2705039-kristy?shelf=i-think-you-should-read-this">i-think-you-should-read-this</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426585900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1314233933628249814">I have just died and gone to Malachi heaven.<br/><br/>I needed this book, I have been in a tragic state of book slumpage. This was a nice dose of pick-me-up (yes, even though it's a book about suicide.)<br/><br/><br/>Super Basic synopsis:<br/><br/>Lela is a tough, rough-n-tumble, foster child. Her life has been pretty dreadful, from bouncing around foster homes, to having no friends, to having her step-father do some pretty heinous acts. She reaches her boiling point and tries to end it all, only he will not give her the satisfac</span>
  <span id="freeText1314233933628249814" style="display:none">I have just died and gone to Malachi heaven.<br /><br />I needed this book, I have been in a tragic state of book slumpage. This was a nice dose of pick-me-up (yes, even though it's a book about suicide.)<br /><br /><br />Super Basic synopsis:<br /><br />Lela is a tough, rough-n-tumble, foster child. Her life has been pretty dreadful, from bouncing around foster homes, to having no friends, to having her step-father do some pretty heinous acts. She reaches her boiling point and tries to end it all, only he will not give her the satisfaction of a release. Her only "salvation" seems to come from her one and only friend, Nadia. When Nadia's tragedy befalls, Lela is broken. Her mind warps, she goes to the suicide gates again, through Nadia. She chooses to save her friend. She will get her out of this horrible place. With the help of some new "friends" she finds her path is not always as black and white as it once appeared. Lela has to make some pretty rough decisions. Can she help her friend escape? Will she get sucked in? How selfless can one person be?<br /><br /><br /><br />Spoilers ahead:<br /><br />I loved this book. I am sad it's over. I want more. Malachi is up there with some of my favorite male book characters.<br /><br /><br />My biggest issue was everytime I read Lela's name, I thought of <a href="http://images.search.yahoo.com/images/view;_ylt=A0PDoV2kZIVQWSsA.zCJzbkF;_ylu=X3oDMTBlMTQ4cGxyBHNlYwNzcgRzbGsDaW1n?back=http%3A%2F%2Fimages.search.yahoo.com%2Fsearch%2Fimages%3Fp%3Dlela%2Bfuturama%26fr%3Dw3i%26fr2%3Dpiv-web%26tab%3Dorganic%26ri%3D3&amp;w=400&amp;h=522&amp;imgurl=images.wikia.com%2Ffuturama%2Fit%2Fimages%2F1%2F10%2FLeela.jpg&amp;rurl=http%3A%2F%2Fit.futurama.wikia.com%2Fwiki%2FTuranga_Leela&amp;size=26.2+KB&amp;name=Turanga+Leela+-+%3Cb%3EFuturama+%3C%2Fb%3EItalia+Wiki&amp;p=lela+futurama&amp;oid=23ac7cf0d99b0edacd8b9c862774aa4d&amp;fr2=piv-web&amp;fr=w3i&amp;tt=Turanga%2BLeela%2B-%2B%253Cb%253EFuturama%2B%253C%252Fb%253EItalia%2BWiki&amp;b=0&amp;ni=21&amp;no=3&amp;ts=&amp;tab=organic&amp;sigr=11f7v3slh&amp;sigb=13021mrbr&amp;sigi=11i36plg2&amp;.crumb=juk.8c7VOPk" rel="nofollow noopener">THIS</a><br /><br />And, I don't think that's where my mind was supposed to be going ;)<br /><br />That flipping ending really worried me as well.... atleast until the last 2 pages. I was worried, now I am just jumping up and down, over the moon, exicted for #2!!!<br /><br />Anwho, I highly suggest you read this one (see, i put it on my "i-think-you-should-read-this shelf). Atleast give it 100 pages or so, before you give up on it as well. Malachi is one character we all need in our lives :)<br /><br /><br />4.5 ah-mazing stars!!!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1314233933628249814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5r0A2VVK3RHr3rIZp5uDObzN7YlYvYNG4nXj0AnSWJpGANzW2tgDFycCmddwbwjoMfcOwnbJ1XdM1ZKB5Bzedw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dJDRPmthVKOWZPP7vdNNsaNr+EDIeEFX5iWDzoIYb53ULQ0x5POKpVq42DVqJ8ZgLlEbC+YMF2ZIhfKfb9bpcA==')})
  }
//]]>
